# Prometheus prometheus-common HTTP Config to TLS Chain

## Your Task

Trace how TLS configuration flows from prometheus/prometheus through prometheus-common to the actual tls.Config used in HTTP clients. Find Go source files in both repos that define, validate, and apply TLSConfig for scrape and remote-write HTTP connections.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo tracing domain.

## Available Resources

No local repositories are pre-checked out.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
*(none — all repos available locally)*

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

## Evaluation

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

  1517→func validateHeadersForTracing(headers map[string]string) error {
  1518→	for header := range headers {
  1519→		if strings.ToLower(header) == "authorization" {
  1520→			return errors.New("custom authorization header configuration is not yet supported")
  1521→		}
  1522→		if _, ok := reservedHeaders[strings.ToLower(header)]; ok {
  1523→			return fmt.Errorf("%s is a reserved header. It must not be changed", header)
  1524→		}
  1525→	}
  1526→	return nil
  1527→}
  1528→
  1529→func validateHeaders(headers map[string]string) error {
  1530→	for header := range headers {
  1531→		if strings.ToLower(header) == "authorization" {
  1532→			return errors.New("authorization header must be changed via the basic_auth, authorization, oauth2, sigv4, azuread or google_iam parameter")
  1533→		}
  1534→		if _, ok := reservedHeaders[strings.ToLower(header)]; ok {
  1535→			return fmt.Errorf("%s is a reserved header. It must not be changed", header)
  1536→		}
  1537→	}
  1538→	return nil
  1539→}

Perfect! I've completed the analysis and created `/workspace/answer.json` with comprehensive findings about how TLS configuration flows from prometheus/prometheus through prometheus-common to the actual tls.Config.

## Summary

The TLS configuration trace reveals the following flow:

**1. Configuration Definition** (prometheus/prometheus/config/config.go):
   - `ScrapeConfig`, `RemoteWriteConfig`, `RemoteReadConfig`, `AlertmanagerConfig`, and `TracingConfig` all embed `github.com/prometheus/common/config.HTTPClientConfig` or `config.TLSConfig`

**2. Configuration Validation**:
   - Validation occurs during YAML parsing with `HTTPClientConfig.Validate()` calls
   - File paths are resolved via `SetDirectory()` methods

**3. TLS Application Points**:
   - **Scrape clients**: `scrape/scrape.go` → `newScrapeClient()` → `config_util.NewClientFromConfig()`
   - **Remote write/read**: `storage/remote/client.go` → `NewWriteClient()` / `NewReadClient()` → `config_util.NewClientFromConfig()`
   - **Alertmanagers**: `notifier/alertmanagerset.go` → `config_util.NewClientFromConfig()`
   - **Tracing**: `tracing/tracing.go` → `config_util.NewTLSConfig()` → credentials.NewTLS()
   - **Service Discovery**: Multiple discovery providers use either `NewClientFromConfig()` or `NewTLSConfig()` directly

**4. prometheus-common Core Functions**:
   - `config.NewClientFromConfig()`: Creates HTTP client with full TLS configuration
   - `config.NewTLSConfig()`: Converts prometheus-common TLSConfig to Go's crypto/tls.Config

The answer.json file includes 22 key files from prometheus/prometheus, 14+ relevant symbols, the complete call chain, and a detailed narrative explaining the entire flow.
